     <p>
      <b>
       GNOME
      </b>
      (pronounced
      <span class="nowrap">
       <span class="IPA nopopups">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">
         /
         <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
          <span title="'g' in 'guy'">
           
          </span>
          <span title="// primary stress follows">
           
          </span>
          <span title="'n' in 'no'">
           n
          </span>
          <span title="/o/ long 'o' in 'code'">
           o
          </span>
          <span title="'m' in 'my'">
           m
          </span>
         </span>
         /
        </a>
       </span>
      </span>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      or
      <span class="nowrap">
       <span class="IPA nopopups">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">
         /
         <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
          <span title="// primary stress follows">
           
          </span>
          <span title="'n' in 'no'">
           n
          </span>
          <span title="/o/ long 'o' in 'code'">
           o
          </span>
          <span title="'m' in 'my'">
           m
          </span>
         </span>
         /
        </a>
       </span>
      </span>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ) is a
      <a href="/wiki/Desktop_environment" title="Desktop environment">
       desktop environment
      </a>
      which is composed entirely of
      <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">
       free and open-source software
      </a>
      . Its target
      <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">
       operating system
      </a>
      is
      <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">
       Linux
      </a>
      , but it is also supported on most
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BSD#Significant_BSD_descendants" title="BSD">
       derivatives of BSD
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      GNOME is developed by
      <a href="/wiki/The_GNOME_Project" title="The GNOME Project">
       The GNOME Project
      </a>
      , which is composed of both volunteers and paid contributors, the largest corporate contributor being
      <a href="/wiki/Red_Hat" title="Red Hat">
       Red Hat
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is an international project that aims to develop
      <a href="/wiki/Software_framework" title="Software framework">
       software frameworks
      </a>
      for the development of software, to program end-user applications based on these frameworks, and to coordinate efforts for
      <a href="/wiki/Internationalization_and_localization" title="Internationalization and localization">
       internationalization and localization
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Accessibility" title="Accessibility">
       accessibility
      </a>
      of that software.
     </p>
     <p>
      GNOME is part of the
      <a href="/wiki/GNU_Project" title="GNU Project">
       GNU Project
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Design">
       Design
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Design">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      GNOME aims to be simple and easy to use.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="GNOME_Shell">
       GNOME Shell
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: GNOME Shell">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <table style="border:1px solid #ccc; float:right;">
      <tr>
       <td align="center">
        <div style="position:relative; left:0px; top:0px; width:400px; height:225px">

     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Shell" title="GNOME Shell">
       GNOME Shell
      </a>
      is the official
      <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">
       user interface
      </a>
      of the GNOME desktop environment. It features a top bar holding (from left to right) an Activities button, an application menu, a clock and an integrated system status menu.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gnomeshellterminology_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gnomeshellterminology-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gnome310releasenotes_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gnome310releasenotes-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The application menu displays the name of the application in focus and provides access to functions such as accessing the application's preferences, closing the application, or creating a new application window. The status menu holds various system status indicators, shortcuts to system settings, and session actions including logging out, switching users, locking the screen, and suspending the computer.
     </p>
     <p>
      Clicking on the Activities button, moving the mouse to the top-left hot corner or pressing the
      <a href="/wiki/Super_key_(keyboard_button)" title="Super key (keyboard button)">
       Super key
      </a>
      brings up the Overview.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Overview gives users an overview of current activities and provides a way to switch between windows and workspaces and to launch applications. The Dash on the left houses shortcuts to favorite applications and open windows and an application picker button to show a list of all installed applications.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gnomeshellterminology_12-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-gnomeshellterminology-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A search bar appears at the top and a workspace list for switching between workspaces is on the right. Notifications appear from the bottom of the screen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GNOME_3_classic_mode.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1680" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/GNOME_3_classic_mode.png/220px-GNOME_3_classic_mode.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/GNOME_3_classic_mode.png/330px-GNOME_3_classic_mode.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/GNOME_3_classic_mode.png/440px-GNOME_3_classic_mode.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GNOME_3_classic_mode.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        GNOME 3 Classic Mode
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Beginning with GNOME 3.8, GNOME provides a Classic Mode for those who prefer a traditional desktop experience (similar to GNOME 2).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Compatibility">
       Compatibility
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Compatibility">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      For Linux distributions using GNOME, see
      <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_Linux_distributions" title="Comparison of Linux distributions">
       Comparison of Linux distributions
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <p>
      GNOME runs on the
      <a href="/wiki/X_Window_System" title="X Window System">
       X Window System
      </a>
      and as of GNOME 3.10 also on
      <a href="/wiki/Wayland_(display_server_protocol)" title="Wayland (display server protocol)">
       Wayland
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gnome310releasenotes_13-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-gnome310releasenotes-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Versions of GNOME are available in most
      <a href="/wiki/Linux_distribution" title="Linux distribution">
       Linux distributions
      </a>
      either as the default desktop environment or as an installable option and also in the
      <a href="/wiki/Ports_collection" title="Ports collection">
       ports collections
      </a>
      of most
      <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_Software_Distribution" title="Berkeley Software Distribution">
       BSDs
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In May 2011
      <a href="/wiki/Lennart_Poettering" title="Lennart Poettering">
       Lennart Poettering
      </a>
      proposed
      <a href="/wiki/Systemd" title="Systemd">
       systemd
      </a>
      as a GNOME dependency.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As systemd is available only on Linux, the proposal led to a discussion of possibly dropping support for other platforms in future GNOME releases. Since GNOME 3.2
      <a href="/wiki/Multiseat_configuration" title="Multiseat configuration">
       multiseat
      </a>
      support has been only available on systems using systemd.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gnome32releasenotes_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gnome32releasenotes-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In November 2012 the GNOME release team concluded that systemd can be relied upon for non-basic functionality.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Human_Interface_Guidelines">
       Human Interface Guidelines
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Human Interface Guidelines">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a class="external text" href="https://developer.gnome.org/hig/stable/" rel="nofollow">
       The Official GNOME Human Interface Guidelines
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Since GNOME 2, usability has been a key focus for GNOME. To this end, the GNOME
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_Interface_Guidelines" title="Human Interface Guidelines">
       Human Interface Guidelines
      </a>
      (HIG) were created. All GNOME programs share a common
      <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">
       graphical user interface
      </a>
      (GUI), which is not limited to the employment of the same
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GUI_widget" title="GUI widget">
       GUI widgets
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2014)">
          clarification needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Rather, the design of the GNOME GUI is guided by concepts described in the GNOME HIG, itself relying on insights from
      <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_ergonomics" title="Cognitive ergonomics">
       cognitive ergonomics
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Following the HIG, developers can create high-quality, consistent, and usable GUI programs, as it addresses everything from GUI design to recommended pixel-based layout of widgets.
     </p>
     <p>
      During the GNOME 2 rewrite, many settings deemed of little value to the majority of users were removed.
      <a href="/wiki/Havoc_Pennington" title="Havoc Pennington">
       Havoc Pennington
      </a>
      summarized the usability work in his 2002 essay "Free Software UI", emphasizing the idea that all preferences have a cost, and it is better to make software behave correctly by default than to add a UI preference to get the desired behavior:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       A traditional free software application is configurable so that it has the union of all features anyone's ever seen in any equivalent application on any other historical platform. Or even configurable to be the union of all applications that anyone's ever seen on any historical platform (
       <a href="/wiki/Emacs" title="Emacs">
        Emacs
       </a>
       *cough*).
       <br/>
       Does this hurt anything? Yes it does. It turns out that preferences have a cost. Of course, some preferences also have important benefits  and can be crucial interface features. But each one has a price, and you have to carefully consider its value. Many users and developers don't understand this, and end up with a lot of cost and little value for their preferences dollar.
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       
       <a href="/wiki/Havoc_Pennington" title="Havoc Pennington">
        Havoc Pennington
       </a>
       ,
       <cite>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
         <a href="#cite_note-21">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          21
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </cite>
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Accessibility">
       Accessibility
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Accessibility">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      GNOME aims to make and keep the desktop environment
      <a href="/wiki/Human_factors_and_ergonomics" title="Human factors and ergonomics">
       physically
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_ergonomics" title="Cognitive ergonomics">
       cognitively ergonomic
      </a>
      for people with
      <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">
       disabilities
      </a>
      . The GNOME HIG tries to take this into account as far as possible but specific issues are solved by special software.
     </p>
     <p>
      GNOME addresses
      <a href="/wiki/Computer_accessibility" title="Computer accessibility">
       computer accessibility
      </a>
      issues by using the
      <a href="/wiki/Accessibility_Toolkit" title="Accessibility Toolkit">
       Accessibility Toolkit
      </a>
      (ATK)
      <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" title="Application programming interface">
       application programming interface
      </a>
      , which allows enhancing user experience by using special
      <a href="/wiki/Input_method" title="Input method">
       input methods
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Speech_synthesis" title="Speech synthesis">
       speech synthesis
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Speech_recognition" title="Speech recognition">
       speech recognition
      </a>
      software. Particular utilities are registered with ATK using
      <a href="/wiki/Assistive_Technology_Service_Provider_Interface" title="Assistive Technology Service Provider Interface">
       Assistive Technology Service Provider Interface
      </a>
      (AT-SPI), and become globally used throughout the desktop. Several assistive technology providers, including
      <a href="/wiki/Orca_(assistive_technology)" title="Orca (assistive technology)">
       Orca
      </a>
      screen reader and
      <a href="/wiki/Dasher_(software)" title="Dasher (software)">
       Dasher
      </a>
      input method, were developed specifically for use with GNOME.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">
       Applications
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Applications">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <div style="width:52px">

         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         This section
         <b>
          does not
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
           cite
          </a>
          any
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
           references or sources
          </a>
         </b>
         .
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          Please help improve this section by
          <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing/1">

          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Core_Applications">
       Core Applications
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Core Applications">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Core_Applications" title="GNOME Core Applications">
       GNOME Core Applications
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      There are countless
      <a href="/wiki/GTK%2B" title="GTK+">
       GTK+
      </a>
      - and
      <a href="/wiki/Clutter_(software)" title="Clutter (software)">
       Clutter
      </a>
      -based programs written by various authors. Since the release of GNOME 3.0,
      <a href="/wiki/The_GNOME_Project" title="The GNOME Project">
       The GNOME Project
      </a>
      concentrates on developing a set of programs that accounts for the GNOME Core Applications. All programs that form the GNOME Core Applications have a certain design and the tight integration with one another in common. Some programs are simply renamed existing programs with a revamped user interface, while others have been written from scratch.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Games">
       Games
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Games">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Games" title="GNOME Games">
       GNOME Games
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      GNOME Games have the look and feel of the GNOME Core Applications and are released simultaneously with GNOME. All have been rewritten conforming to the current GNOME Human Interface Guidelines.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Development_Tools">
       Development Tools
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Development Tools">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Anjuta" title="Anjuta">
       Anjuta
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Integrated_development_environment" title="Integrated development environment">
       integrated development environment
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Glade_Interface_Designer" title="Glade Interface Designer">
       Glade
      </a>
      user interface construction tool and
      <a href="/wiki/Devhelp" title="Devhelp">
       Devhelp
      </a>
      API browser were created to provide development tools consistent with the GNOME desktop and to facilitate the development of GNOME software. The
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Accerciser&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Accerciser (page does not exist)">
       Accerciser
      </a>
      accessibility explorer and several debugging tools, including
      <a href="/wiki/Nemiver" title="Nemiver">
       Nemiver
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=GtkInspector&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="GtkInspector (page does not exist)">
       GtkInspector
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alleyoop_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alleyoop (software) (page does not exist)">
       Alleyoop
      </a>
      , have also been provided to facilitate development of GNOME software.
     </p>
     <p>
      Integration options for third-party development tools (e.g.
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=NoFlo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="NoFlo (page does not exist)">
       NoFlo
      </a>
      ) also exist.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Development">
       Development
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Development">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      GNOME is developed by
      <a href="/wiki/The_GNOME_Project" title="The GNOME Project">
       The GNOME Project
      </a>
      and provides the GNOME Desktop Environment, a
      <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">
       graphical user interface
      </a>
      and a set of core applications, and the GNOME Development Platform, a framework for building applications that integrate with the desktop.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As with most free software projects, GNOME development is loosely managed. Discussion chiefly occurs on a number of public mailing lists.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      GNOME developers and users gather at an annual
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GUADEC" title="GUADEC">
       GUADEC
      </a>
      meeting to discuss the current state and the future direction of GNOME.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      GNOME incorporates standards and programs from
      <a href="/wiki/Freedesktop.org" title="Freedesktop.org">
       freedesktop.org
      </a>
      to better
      <a href="/wiki/Interoperability" title="Interoperability">
       interoperate
      </a>
      with other desktops.
     </p>
     <p>
      GNOME is mainly written in
      <a href="/wiki/C_(programming_language)" title="C (programming language)">
       C
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">
       C++
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Vala_(programming_language)" title="Vala (programming language)">
       Vala
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">
       Python
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">
       JavaScript
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gnomelanguages_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-gnomelanguages-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A number of
      <a href="/wiki/Language_binding" title="Language binding">
       language bindings
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_language_bindings_for_GTK%2B" title="List of language bindings for GTK+">
       are available
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Release_cycle">
       Release cycle
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Release cycle">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Each of the component software products in the GNOME project has its own version number and
      <a href="/wiki/Software_release_life_cycle" title="Software release life cycle">
       release schedule
      </a>
      . However, individual module maintainers coordinate their efforts to create a full GNOME stable release on an approximately six-month schedule. Some experimental projects are excluded from these releases.
     </p>
     <p>
      GNOME releases are made to the main FTP server in the form of
      <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">
       source code
      </a>
      with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Configure_(computing)" title="Configure (computing)">
       configure
      </a>
      scripts, which are compiled by operating system vendors and integrated with the rest of their systems before distribution. Most vendors use only stable and tested versions of GNOME, and provide it in the form of easily installed, pre-compiled packages. The source code of every stable and development version of GNOME is stored in the GNOME
      <a href="/wiki/Git_(software)" title="Git (software)">
       git
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Source_code_repository" title="Source code repository">
       source code repository
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      A number of build-
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scripting_programming_language" title="Scripting programming language">
       scripts
      </a>
      (such as
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=JHBuild&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="JHBuild (page does not exist)">
       JHBuild
      </a>
      or formerly
      <a href="/wiki/GARNOME" title="GARNOME">
       GARNOME
      </a>
      ) are available to help automate the process of compiling the source code.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Development_platform">
       Development platform
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Development platform">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/GLib" title="GLib">
       GLib
      </a>
      data structures and utilities library,
      <a href="/wiki/GObject" title="GObject">
       GObject
      </a>
      object and type system and
      <a href="/wiki/GTK%2B" title="GTK+">
       GTK+
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Widget_toolkit" title="Widget toolkit">
       widget toolkit
      </a>
      comprise the central part of GNOME development platform. This foundation is further extended with
      <a href="/wiki/D-Bus" title="D-Bus">
       D-Bus
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Inter-process_communication" title="Inter-process communication">
       IPC
      </a>
      framework,
      <a href="/wiki/Cairo_(graphics)" title="Cairo (graphics)">
       Cairo
      </a>
      2D vector-based drawing library,
      <a href="/wiki/Clutter_(software)" title="Clutter (software)">
       Clutter
      </a>
      accelerated graphics library,
      <a href="/wiki/Pango" title="Pango">
       Pango
      </a>
      international text rendering library,
      <a href="/wiki/PulseAudio" title="PulseAudio">
       PulseAudio
      </a>
      low-level audio
      <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" title="Application programming interface">
       API
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/GStreamer" title="GStreamer">
       GStreamer
      </a>
      multimedia framework, and several specialized libraries including
      <a href="/wiki/NetworkManager" title="NetworkManager">
       NetworkManager
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/PackageKit" title="PackageKit">
       PackageKit
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Telepathy_(software)" title="Telepathy (software)">
       Telepathy
      </a>
      (instant messaging) and
      <a href="/wiki/WebKit" title="WebKit">
       WebKit
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GNOME-escritorio-1.x.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/GNOME-escritorio-1.x.png/220px-GNOME-escritorio-1.x.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/GNOME-escritorio-1.x.png/330px-GNOME-escritorio-1.x.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/GNOME-escritorio-1.x.png/440px-GNOME-escritorio-1.x.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GNOME-escritorio-1.x.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        GNOME 1, 1999
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_free_and_open-source_software#Desktop_.281984-.29" title="History of free and open-source software">
       History of free and open-source software: Desktop
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      GNOME was started in August 1997 by
      <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Icaza" title="Miguel de Icaza">
       Miguel de Icaza
      </a>
      and Federico Mena
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      as a
      <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">
       free software
      </a>
      project to develop a
      <a href="/wiki/Desktop_environment" title="Desktop environment">
       desktop environment
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Application_software" title="Application software">
       applications
      </a>
      for it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was founded in part because
      <a href="/wiki/K_Desktop_Environment_1" title="K Desktop Environment 1">
       K Desktop Environment
      </a>
      , an already existing free software desktop environment, relied on the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qt_(toolkit)" title="Qt (toolkit)">
       Qt
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Widget_toolkit" title="Widget toolkit">
       widget toolkit
      </a>
      which used a
      <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">
       proprietary software
      </a>
      license until version 2.0 (June 1999).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In place of Qt, the
      <a href="/wiki/GTK%2B" title="GTK+">
       GTK+
      </a>
      toolkit was chosen as the base of GNOME. GTK+ uses the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GNU_Lesser_Public_License" title="GNU Lesser Public License">
       GNU Lesser Public License
      </a>
      (LGPL), a free software license that allows software linking to it to use a much wider set of licenses, including proprietary software licenses.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      GNOME itself is licensed under the LGPL for its libraries, and the
      <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">
       GNU General Public License
      </a>
      (GPL) for its applications.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The name "GNOME" was initially an acronym of
      <i>
       GNU Network Object Model Environment
      </i>
      , referring to the original intention of creating a
      <a href="/wiki/Distributed_object" title="Distributed object">
       distributed object
      </a>
      framework similar to
      <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">
       Microsoft
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Object_Linking_and_Embedding" title="Object Linking and Embedding">
       OLE
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but the acronym was eventually dropped because it no longer reflected the vision of the GNOME project.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The California startup
      <a href="/wiki/Eazel" title="Eazel">
       Eazel
      </a>
      developed the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nautilus_(file_manager)" title="Nautilus (file manager)">
       Nautilus file manager
      </a>
      from 1999 to 2001. De Icaza and
      <a href="/wiki/Nat_Friedman" title="Nat Friedman">
       Nat Friedman
      </a>
      founded Helix Code (later
      <a href="/wiki/Ximian" title="Ximian">
       Ximian
      </a>
      ) in 1999 in Massachusetts. The company developed GNOME's infrastructure and applications, and in 2003 was purchased by
      <a href="/wiki/Novell" title="Novell">
       Novell
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <span id="GNOME_Office">
      </span>
      During the transition to GNOME 2 around the year 2001 and shortly thereafter there were brief talks about creating a
      <i>
       GNOME Office
      </i>
      suite.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On September 15, 2003 GNOME-Office 1.0, consisting of
      <a href="/wiki/AbiWord" title="AbiWord">
       AbiWord
      </a>
      2.0,
      <a href="/wiki/GNOME-DB" title="GNOME-DB">
       GNOME-DB
      </a>
      1.0 and
      <a href="/wiki/Gnumeric" title="Gnumeric">
       Gnumeric
      </a>
      1.2.0 was released.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although some release planning for GNOME Office 1.2 was happening on gnome-office mailing list,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Gnumeric 1.4 was announced as a part of it,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the 1.2 release of the suite itself was never announced. As of May 4, 2014
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      GNOME wiki only mentions "GNOME/Gtk applications that are useful in an office environment".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gnome-2.0.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/Gnome-2.0.jpg/220px-Gnome-2.0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/Gnome-2.0.jpg/330px-Gnome-2.0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/Gnome-2.0.jpg/440px-Gnome-2.0.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gnome-2.0.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        GNOME 2.0, June 2002
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="GNOME_2">
       GNOME 2
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: GNOME 2">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      GNOME 2 was very similar to a conventional desktop interface, featuring a simple desktop in which users could interact with virtual objects, such as windows, icons, and files. GNOME 2 used
      <a href="/wiki/Metacity" title="Metacity">
       Metacity
      </a>
      as its default
      <a href="/wiki/Window_manager" title="Window manager">
       window manager
      </a>
      . The handling of windows, applications, and files in GNOME 2 is similar to that of contemporary desktop operating systems. In the default configuration of GNOME 2, the desktop has a launcher menu for quick access to installed programs and file locations; open windows may be accessed by a taskbar along the bottom of the screen, and the top-right corner features a notification area for programs to display notices while running in the background. However, these features can be moved to almost any position or orientation the user desires, replaced with other functions or removed altogether.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="GNOME_3">
       GNOME 3
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: GNOME 3">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Before GNOME 3, GNOME used the traditional
      <a href="/wiki/Desktop_metaphor" title="Desktop metaphor">
       desktop metaphor
      </a>
      , but in GNOME 3 this was replaced with
      <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Shell" title="GNOME Shell">
       GNOME Shell
      </a>
      , a more abstract metaphor where switching between different tasks and virtual workspaces takes place in a separate area called Overview. Also, since
      <a href="/wiki/Mutter_(software)" title="Mutter (software)">
       Mutter
      </a>
      replaced Metacity as the default window manager, the minimize and maximize buttons no longer appear on the titlebar by default.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adwaita_(software)" title="Adwaita (software)">
       Adwaita
      </a>
      replaced
      <a href="/wiki/Clearlooks" title="Clearlooks">
       Clearlooks
      </a>
      as the default theme. Many
      <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Core_Applications" title="GNOME Core Applications">
       GNOME Core Applications
      </a>
      also went through redesigns to provide a more consistent user experience.
     </p>
     <p>
      These major changes initially evoked widespread criticism. The
      <a href="/wiki/MATE_(software)" title="MATE (software)">
       MATE desktop environment
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Fork_(software_development)" title="Fork (software development)">
       forked
      </a>
      from the GNOME 2 codebase with the intent of retaining the traditional GNOME 2 interface while keeping it compatible with modern Linux technology, such as
      <a href="/wiki/GTK%2B" title="GTK+">
       GTK+
      </a>
      3. The
      <a href="/wiki/Linux_Mint" title="Linux Mint">
       Linux Mint
      </a>
      team addressed the issue in another way by developing the "Mint GNOME Shell Extensions," extensions that ran on top of GNOME 3. These extensions allowed GNOME 3 to be used via the traditional desktop metaphor. This eventually led to the creation of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cinnamon_(user_interface)" title="Cinnamon (user interface)">
       Cinnamon user interface
      </a>
      , which was forked from the GNOME 3 codebase.
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2015, critical reception is much more positive.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pcworld_47-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pcworld-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Debian" title="Debian">
       Debian
      </a>
      , a Linux distribution that had historically used GNOME 2, switched to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/XFCE" title="XFCE">
       XFCE
      </a>
      when GNOME 3 was released. However, Debian developers are planning to switch back to GNOME 3 with their next release.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-varguy_48-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-varguy-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pcworld_47-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-pcworld-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Linus_Torvalds" title="Linus Torvalds">
       Linus Torvalds
      </a>
      , the creator of the Linux kernel, switched back to GNOME 3 in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pcworld_47-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-pcworld-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On May 13 2015, the GNOME Project released a maintenance update for GNOME 3.16.2 desktop environment, GNOME 3.16.2 is the last official maintenance release for the GNOME 3.16 desktop environment, this update provided many bug fixes, documentation improvements, and translation updates.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The next major version due for release on September 23 2015, will be GNOME 3.18., which Georges Stavacas says will include improved features. Specifically highlighting that Calendar, Files, an improved sidebar, bookmark management will be redefined, and a new dialog for renaming and creating folders and files will become available.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

       <td>
        Addition of
        <a href="/wiki/Cheese_(software)" title="Cheese (software)">
         Cheese
        </a>
        , a tool for taking photos from webcams and
        <a href="/wiki/Vinagre" title="Vinagre">
         Remote Desktop Viewer
        </a>
        ; basic window compositing support in
        <a href="/wiki/Metacity" title="Metacity">
         Metacity
        </a>
        ; introduction of
        <a href="/wiki/GVFS" title="GVFS">
         GVFS
        </a>
        ; improved playback support for DVDs and
        <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">
         YouTube
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/MythTV" title="MythTV">
         MythTV
        </a>
        support in Totem; internationalised clock applet; Google Calendar support and message tagging in
        <a href="/wiki/Evolution_(software)" title="Evolution (software)">
         Evolution
        </a>
        ; improvements in Evince, Tomboy, Sound Juicer and Calculator.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
         <a href="#cite_note-66">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          66
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        2.24
       </th>
       <td>
        September 2008
       </td>
       <td>
        Addition of the Empathy instant messenger client,
        <a href="/wiki/Ekiga" title="Ekiga">
         Ekiga
        </a>
        3.0, tabbed browsing in Nautilus, better multiple screens support and improved digital TV support.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
         <a href="#cite_note-67">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          67
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        2.26
       </th>
       <td>
        March 2009
       </td>
       <td>
        New optical disc recording application
        <a href="/wiki/Brasero_(software)" title="Brasero (software)">
         Brasero
        </a>
        , simpler file sharing, media player improvements, support for
        <a href="/wiki/Multi-monitor" title="Multi-monitor">
         multiple monitors
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fingerprint_reader" title="Fingerprint reader">
         fingerprint reader
        </a>
        support.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
         <a href="#cite_note-68">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          68
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        2.28
       </th>
       <td>
        September 2009
       </td>
       <td>
        Addition of GNOME Bluetooth module. Improvements to Epiphany web browser, Empathy instant messenger client, Time Tracker, and accessibility. Upgrade to
        <a href="/wiki/GTK%2B" title="GTK+">
         GTK+
        </a>
        version 2.18.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
         <a href="#cite_note-69">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          69
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        2.30
       </th>
       <td>
        March 2010
       </td>
       <td>
        Improvements to Nautilus file manager, Empathy instant messenger client, Tomboy, Evince, Time Tracker, Epiphany, and
        <a href="/wiki/Vinagre" title="Vinagre">
         Vinagre
        </a>
        . iPod and iPod Touch devices are now partially supported via GVFS through libimobiledevice. Uses
        <a href="/wiki/GTK%2B" title="GTK+">
         GTK+
        </a>
        2.20.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
         <a href="#cite_note-70">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          70
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        2.32
       </th>
       <td>
        September 2010
       </td>
       <td>
        Addition of Rygel and GNOME Color Manager. Improvements to Empathy instant messenger client, Evince, Nautilus file manager and others. 3.0 was intended to be released in September 2010, so a large part of the development effort since 2.30 went towards 3.0.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rel2.32_71-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-rel2.32-71">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          71
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th colspan="4" style="background:light-gray">
        GNOME 3
       </th>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        3.0
       </th>
       <td>
        April 2011
       </td>
       <td>
        Introduction of
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Shell" title="GNOME Shell">
         GNOME Shell
        </a>
        . A redesigned settings framework with fewer, more focused options. Topic-oriented help based on the
        <a href="/wiki/Mallard_(documentation)" title="Mallard (documentation)">
         Mallard markup language
        </a>
        . Side-by-side window tiling. A new visual theme and default font. Adoption of GTK+ 3.0 with its improved language bindings, themes, touch, and multiplatform support. Removal of long-deprecated development APIs.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-release-notes-3.0_72-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-release-notes-3.0-72">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          72
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        3.2
       </th>
       <td>
        September 2011
       </td>
       <td>
        Online accounts support; Web applications support; contacts manager; documents and files manager; quick preview of files in the File Manager; greater integration; better documentation; enhanced looks and various performance improvements.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gnome32releasenotes_18-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-gnome32releasenotes-18">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          18
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        3.4
       </th>
       <td>
        March 2012
       </td>
       <td>
        New Look for GNOME 3 Applications: Documents, Epiphany (now called Web), and
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME_Contacts&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="GNOME Contacts (page does not exist)">
         GNOME Contacts
        </a>
        . Search for documents from the Activities overview. Application menus support. Refreshed interface components: New color picker, redesigned scrollbars, easier to use spin buttons, and hideable title bars. Smooth scrolling support. New animated backgrounds. Improved system settings with new Wacom panel. Easier extensions management. Better hardware support. Topic-oriented documentation. Video calling and Live Messenger support in Empathy. Better accessibility: Improved Orca integration, better high contrast mode, and new zoom settings. Plus many other application enhancements and smaller details.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-release-notes-3.4_73-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-release-notes-3.4-73">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          73
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        3.6
       </th>
       <td>
        September 2012
       </td>
       <td>
        Refreshed Core components: New applications button and improved layout in the Activities Overview. A new login and lock screen. Redesigned Message Tray. Notifications are now smarter, more noticeable, easier to dismiss. Improved interface and settings for System Settings. The user menu now shows Power Off by default. Integrated Input Methods. Accessibility is always on. New applications: Boxes, that was introduced as a preview version in GNOME 3.4, and Clocks, an application to handle world times. Updated looks for Disk Usage Analyzer, Empathy and Font Viewer. Improved
        <a href="/wiki/Braille" title="Braille">
         braille
        </a>
        support in
        <a href="/wiki/Orca_(assistive_technology)" title="Orca (assistive technology)">
         Orca
        </a>
        . In Web, the previously blank start page was replaced by a grid that holds your most visited pages, plus better full screen mode and a beta of WebKit2. Evolution renders email using WebKit. Major improvements to Disks. Revamped Files application (also known as Nautilus), with new features like Recent files and search.
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        3.8
       </th>
       <td>
        March 2013
       </td>
       <td>
        Refreshed Core components: A new applications view with frequently used and all apps. An overhauled window layout. New input methods OSD switcher. The Notifications &amp; Messaging tray now react to the force with which the pointer is pressed against the screen edge. Added Classic mode for those who prefer a more traditional desktop experience. The GNOME Settings application features an updated toolbar design. New Initial Setup assistant. GNOME Online Accounts integrates with more services. Web has been upgraded to use the WebKit2 engine. Web has a new private browsing mode. Documents has gained a new dual page mode &amp; Google Documents integration. Improved user interface of Contacts.
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Files" title="GNOME Files">
         GNOME Files
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Boxes" title="GNOME Boxes">
         GNOME Boxes
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Disks" title="GNOME Disks">
         GNOME Disks
        </a>
        have received a number of improvements. Integration of
        <a href="/wiki/OwnCloud" title="OwnCloud">
         ownCloud
        </a>
        . New
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Core_Applications" title="GNOME Core Applications">
         GNOME Core Applications
        </a>
        :
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME_Clocks&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="GNOME Clocks (page does not exist)">
         GNOME Clocks
        </a>
        and
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME_Weather&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="GNOME Weather (page does not exist)">
         GNOME Weather
        </a>
        .
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        3.10
       </th>
       <td>
        September 2013
       </td>
       <td>
        A reworked system status area, which gives a more focused overview of the system. A collection of new applications, including
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME_Maps&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="GNOME Maps (page does not exist)">
         GNOME Maps
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME_Notes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="GNOME Notes (page does not exist)">
         GNOME Notes
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME_Music&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="GNOME Music (page does not exist)">
         GNOME Music
        </a>
        and
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=GNOME_Photos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="GNOME Photos (page does not exist)">
         GNOME Photos
        </a>
        . New geolocation features, such as automatic time zones and world clocks.
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HiDPI" title="HiDPI">
         HiDPI
        </a>
        support
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
         <a href="#cite_note-74">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          74
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        and smart card support.
        <a href="/wiki/D-Bus" title="D-Bus">
         D-Bus
        </a>
        activation made possible with
        <a href="/wiki/GLib" title="GLib">
         GLib
        </a>
        2.38
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
         <a href="#cite_note-75">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          75
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        3.12
       </th>
       <td>
        March 2014
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wallen2014_76-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-wallen2014-76">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          76
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
       <td>
        Improved keyboard navigation and window selection in the Overview. Revamped first set-up utility based on usability tests. Wired networking re-added to the system status area. Customizable application folders in the Applications view. Introduction of new GTK+ widgets such as popovers in many applications. New tab style in GTK+.
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Videos" title="GNOME Videos">
         GNOME Videos
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Terminal" title="GNOME Terminal">
         GNOME Terminal
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Gedit" title="Gedit">
         gedit
        </a>
        were given a fresh look, more consistent with the HIG. A search provider for the terminal emulator is included in
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Shell" title="GNOME Shell">
         GNOME Shell
        </a>
        . Improvements to
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Software" title="GNOME Software">
         GNOME Software
        </a>
        and high-density display support. A new sound recorder application. New desktop notifications API. Progress in the
        <a href="/wiki/Wayland_(display_server_protocol)" title="Wayland (display server protocol)">
         Wayland
        </a>
        port has reached a usable state that can be optionally previewed.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th>
        3.14
       </th>
       <td>
        September 2014
       </td>
       <td>
        Improved desktop environment animations. Improved touchscreen support.
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Software" title="GNOME Software">
         GNOME Software
        </a>
        supports managing installed add-ons. GNOME Photos adds support for
        <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
         Google
        </a>
        . Redesigned UI for
        <a href="/wiki/Evince" title="Evince">
         Evince
        </a>
        , Sudoku, Mines and Weather. Hitori is added as part of
        <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Games" title="GNOME Games">
         GNOME Games
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">

            citation needed

        </sup>
       </td>

      <tr>
       <th>
        3.16
       </th>
       <td>
        March 2015
       </td>
       <td>
        33,000 changes. Major changes include UI color scheme goes from black to charcoal. Overlay scroll bars added. Improvements to notifications including integration with Calendar applet. Tweaks to various apps including Files, Image Viewer, and Maps. Access to Preview Apps. Continued porting from X11 to Wayland.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
